1	"""Regression tests for the bugs fixed alongside this harness (SPEC §3.1, §9).
2	
3	Each would fail on the pre-fix code:
4	  * terminus() session-expiry retry did args.push()/del args[...] on a tuple -> crash.
5	  * check/umich/__init__.py disabled branch called sc.console(...) as if callable -> TypeError.
6	
7	The two non-UMich render-path bugs discovered during implementation (the `contacts`
8	UnboundLocalError and the unconditional `if True:` UMich annual-billing block) are
9	regressed by the offline e2e in tests/e2e/ — it renders under the plugin-disabled config,
10	which crashed on the pre-fix code.
11	"""
12	import importlib.util
13	from importlib.machinery import SourceFileLoader
14	from pathlib import Path
15	
16	import pytest
17	
18	pytestmark = pytest.mark.integration
19	
20	
21	def test_terminus_retries_on_expired_session(psh, monkeypatch):
22	    calls = {"n": 0}
23	
24	    def fake_run_terminus(command, input_data=None):
25	        calls["n"] += 1
26	        if calls["n"] == 1:
27	            return ("", "Invalid or expired session header: X-Pantheon-Session", False)
28	        return ('{"ok": 1}', "", False)
29	
30	    monkeypatch.setattr(psh, "run_terminus", fake_run_terminus)
31	    monkeypatch.setattr(psh.time, "sleep", lambda *_a, **_k: None)
32	
33	    result = psh.terminus("org:site:list", "some-org")
34	    assert result == {"ok": 1}
35	    assert calls["n"] == 2  # original + one retry (pre-fix this path raised on the tuple)
36	
37	
38	def test_terminus_retry_does_not_loop_forever(psh, monkeypatch):
39	    calls = {"n": 0}
40	
41	    def always_expired(command, input_data=None):
42	        calls["n"] += 1
43	        return ("", "Invalid or expired session header: X-Pantheon-Session", False)
44	
45	    monkeypatch.setattr(psh, "run_terminus", always_expired)
46	    monkeypatch.setattr(psh.time, "sleep", lambda *_a, **_k: None)
47	
48	    psh.terminus("org:site:list", "some-org")
49	    assert calls["n"] == 2  # one retry only; the sentinel disables a second retry
50	
51	
52	def test_check_umich_disabled_import_does_not_crash(psh, reset_sc):
53	    sc = reset_sc
54	    sc.config = {}  # UMich absent -> the module's else branch runs sc.console.print(...)
55	    init = Path(psh.__file__).parent / "check" / "umich" / "__init__.py"
56	    loader = SourceFileLoader("check_umich_probe", str(init))
57	    spec = importlib.util.spec_from_loader("check_umich_probe", loader)
58	    module = importlib.util.module_from_spec(spec)
59	    loader.exec_module(module)  # pre-fix: TypeError from sc.console('...'); post-fix: fine
60	    # The disabled (else) branch ran — it only prints — so no check hooks were registered
61	    # (the enabled branch would have added three). This confirms the fixed path executed.
62	    assert sc.hooks["check"] == []
63
```

### ↳ Tool result

```
1	
2	import base64
3	import json
4	
5	import boto3
6	import botocore.exceptions
7	
8	import script_context as sc
9	
10	
11	secrets = {}
12	session = None
13	client = None
14	
15	
16	def get_secret(secret_name, key_name = None, region_name='', profile_name=''):
17	
18	    global secrets, session, client
19	
20	    # Load and cache the secret if it hasn't been loaded yet
21	    if secret_name not in secrets:
22	        sc.debug(f'Loading secret {secret_name} from AWS Secrets Manager')
23	        if profile_name != '':
24	            try:
25	                session = boto3.session.Session(profile_name=profile_name)
26	            except botocore.exceptions.ProfileNotFound:
27	                session = boto3.session.Session()
28	        else:
29	            session = boto3.session.Session()
30	
31	        if region_name != '':
32	            client = session.client(service_name='secretsmanager', region_name=region_name)
33	        else:
34	            client = session.client(service_name='secretsmanager')
35	
36	        # get_secret_value can throw exceptions.  We deliberately do not catch them here.
37	        # See https://docs.aws.amazon.com/secretsmanager/latest/apireference/API_GetSecretValue.html
38	        get_secret_value_response = client.get_secret_value(SecretId=secret_name)
39	
40	        # Decrypts secret using the associated KMS CMK.
41	        # Depending on whether the secret is a string or binary, one of these fields will be populated.
42	        if 'SecretString' in get_secret_value_response:
43	            secret = get_secret_value_response['SecretString']
44	        else:
45	            secret = base64.b64decode(get_secret_value_response['SecretBinary'])
46	
47	        secrets[secret_name] = json.loads(secret)
48	
49	    # Return the requested secret or just the requested key
50	    if key_name is None:
51	        return secrets[secret_name]
52	    if key_name not in secrets[secret_name]:
53	        raise KeyError(f'Key {key_name} not found in secret {secret_name}')
54	    #sc.debug(f'Secret {secret_name}.{key_name}: {secrets[secret_name][key_name]}')
55	    return secrets[secret_name][key_name]
56
```

11	def get_cloudflare_ips():
12	
13	    global cloudflare_ipv4_nets, cloudflare_ipv6_nets
14	
15	    cloudflare = Cloudflare(
16	        api_email=sc.config['Cloudflare']['member_email'],
17	        api_key=sc.config['Cloudflare']['member_api_key']
18	    )
19	
20	    with sc.console.status('[bold green]Getting Cloudflare IP ranges ...'):
21	        try:
22	            cloudflare_ips = cloudflare.ips.list()
23	        except Exception as e:
24	            sys.exit(f'ERROR: Unable to get lists of Cloudflare IPs: {e}')
25	        if sc.options.verbose > 2:
26	            sc.debug('Cloudfare IPs:')
27	            pprint(cloudflare_ips)
28	        sc.plugin_context['plugin.cloudflare']['cloudflare_ipv4_nets'] = [ipaddress.ip_network(cidr) for cidr in cloudflare_ips.ipv4_cidrs]
29	        sc.plugin_context['plugin.cloudflare']['cloudflare_ipv6_nets'] = [ipaddress.ip_network(cidr) for cidr in cloudflare_ips.ipv6_cidrs]

2	import sqlalchemy as db
3	
4	from rich.pretty import pprint
5	
6	import script_context as sc
7	
8	
9	setup_completed = False
10	portal_plan_info = {}
11	
12	
13	def setup_portal_db():
14	    global portal_plan_info, setup_completed
15	    sc.debug('Getting information from portal database')
16	    portal_sites = {}
17	    db_info = sc.config['UMich']['portal']['db']
18	    portal_db_engine = db.create_engine(f'mysql+mysqldb://{db_info["user"]}:{db_info["password"]}@'
19	                                        f'{db_info["host"]}:{db_info["port"]}/{db_info["name"]}',
20	                                        echo=True if sc.options.verbose >= 2 else False)
21	
22	    with portal_db_engine.connect() as connection:
23	        metadata = db.MetaData()
24	
25	        sites_site = db.Table('sites_site', metadata, autoload_with=portal_db_engine)
26	        query = db.select(sites_site.c['id', 'site_slug', 'owner_group', 'shortcode'])
27	        for row in connection.execute(query).all():
28	            # https://github.com/sqlalchemy/sqlalchemy/discussions/10091
29	            # noinspection PyProtectedMember
30	            site = row._asdict()
31	            portal_sites[site['site_slug']] = {
32	                'id': site['id'],
33	                'owner_group': site['owner_group'],
34	                'shortcode': site['shortcode'],
35	            }
36	
37	        sc.config['Pantheon']['plan_sku_to_name'] = {}
38	        sites_pantheonplan = db.Table('sites_pantheonplan', metadata, autoload_with=portal_db_engine)
39	        query = db.select(sites_pantheonplan.c[
40	                              'portal_plan_name',
41	                              'pantheon_plan_sku',
42	                              'traffic_limits',
43	                              'annual_plan_customer_charge',
44	                              'is_active'])
45	        for row in connection.execute(query).all():
46	            # noinspection PyProtectedMember
47	            plan = row._asdict()
48	            if plan['is_active']:
49	                if plan['portal_plan_name'] not in portal_plan_info:
50	                    portal_plan_info[plan['portal_plan_name']] = {}
51	                portal_plan_info[plan['portal_plan_name']]['traffic_limit'] = str(plan['traffic_limits'])
52	                portal_plan_info[plan['portal_plan_name']]['cost'] = str(plan['annual_plan_customer_charge'])
53	            sc.config['Pantheon']['plan_sku_to_name'][plan['pantheon_plan_sku']] = plan['portal_plan_name']
54	
55	        sc.invoke_hooks('setup.umich.portal', connection)
56	
57	    portal_db_engine.dispose()
58	
59	    sc.config['UMich']['portal']['sites'] = portal_sites
60	
61	    if sc.options.verbose >= 2:
62	        pprint(portal_sites)
63	        pprint(portal_plan_info)
64	        pprint(sc.config['Pantheon']['plan_sku_to_name'])
65	
66	    setup_completed = True
67	    return
68	
69	
70	def plan_info(plan: str, field: str) -> str:
71	    if not setup_completed:
72	        return '<{umich portal plan_info ' + f'"{plan}" {field}' + '}'
73	    return portal_plan_info[plan][field]

10	import sqlalchemy as db

13	import script_context as sc
14	
15	
16	GAUGE_PIXELS_WIDTH = 128
17	GAUGE_PIXELS_HEIGHT = 128
18	
19	GOOD_SCORE_MIN = 90
20	OK_SCORE_MIN = 50
21	
22	NO_SCORE_COLOR   = '#888888'  # --rating-color-default
23	
24	GOOD_SCORE_COLOR = '#00CC66'  # --rating-color-good
25	OK_SCORE_COLOR   = '#FFAA33'  # --rating-color-ok
26	BAD_SCORE_COLOR  = '#FF3333'  # --rating-color-bad

31	sitelens_configured_scans_by_site = {}
32	sitelens_scores = {}
33	
34	
35	def setup_sitelens(connection) -> None:
36	    sc.debug('Getting SiteLens information from portal database')
37	    global sitelens_configured_scans_by_site, sitelens_scores
38	
39	    site_url_scan_config = db.Table('sites_siteurlscanconfiguration', db.MetaData(), autoload_with=connection)
40	    sites_lighthousescanresult = db.Table('sites_lighthousescanresult', db.MetaData(), autoload_with=connection)
41	
42	    # Get the configuration ids of what will be scanned for each site
43	    query = db.select(site_url_scan_config.c.site_id, site_url_scan_config.c.id)
44	
45	    for row in connection.execute(query).all():
46	        # https://github.com/sqlalchemy/sqlalchemy/discussions/10091
47	        # noinspection PyProtectedMember
48	        site = row._asdict()
49	        if site['site_id'] not in sitelens_configured_scans_by_site:
50	            sitelens_configured_scans_by_site[site['site_id']] = [site['id']]
51	        else:
52	            sitelens_configured_scans_by_site[site['site_id']].append(site['id'])
53	
54	    if sc.options.verbose >= 3:
55	        sc.console.print('SiteLens configurations by site:')
56	        pprint(sitelens_configured_scans_by_site)
57	
58	    # Get the latest scores by running the SQL query
59	    #
60	    # SELECT configuration_id, timestamp, accessibility_score, performance_score, best_practices_score, seo_score
61	    # FROM sites_lighthousescanresult AS t1
62	    # WHERE timestamp = (
63	    #     SELECT MAX(timestamp) FROM sites_lighthousescanresult AS t2
64	    #     WHERE t1.configuration_id = t2.configuration_id
65	    # );
66	    #
67	    t1 = sites_lighthousescanresult.alias('t1')
68	    t2 = sites_lighthousescanresult.alias('t2')
69	
70	    subquery = db.select(db.func.max(t2.c.timestamp)
71	                         ).where(t1.c.configuration_id == t2.c.configuration_id).scalar_subquery()
72	    query = db.select(
73	        t1.c.configuration_id,
74	        t1.c.timestamp,
75	        t1.c.accessibility_score,
76	        t1.c.performance_score,
77	        t1.c.best_practices_score,
78	        t1.c.seo_score,
79	    ).where(t1.c.timestamp == subquery)
80	
81	    for row in connection.execute(query).all():
82	        # https://github.com/sqlalchemy/sqlalchemy/discussions/10091
83	        # noinspection PyProtectedMember
84	        scores = row._asdict()
85	        sitelens_scores[scores['configuration_id']] = scores
86	
87	    sc.debug(f'Loaded {len(sitelens_scores)} SiteLens scores')
88	
89	
90	def check_sitelens_urls(site_context) -> None:
91	    sc.debug('Checking if SiteLens URLs have been configured')
92	    site_name = site_context['site']['name']
93	    portal_sites = sc.config['UMich']['portal']['sites']
94	
95	    if site_name not in portal_sites:
96	        sc.console.print(f'[bold red]ERROR: Site {site_name} is not in the portal database')
97	        return
98	
99	    portal_site_id = portal_sites[site_name]['id']
100	    if portal_site_id not in sitelens_configured_scans_by_site:
101	        sc.console.print(f'[bold red]Site {site_name} has no SiteLens configurations, skipping SiteLens checks')
102	        return
103	
104	    num_paths_configured = len(sitelens_configured_scans_by_site[portal_site_id])
105	    if num_paths_configured >= 4:
106	        sc.debug(f'[green]{site_name} has {num_paths_configured} SiteLens paths configured')
107	        return
108	
109	    sc.debug(f'[red]NOTE: {site_name} only has {num_paths_configured} SiteLens paths configured')
110	    sc.add_notice({
111	        'type': 'info',
112	        'csv': f'{site_name},sitelens-url-paths,{num_paths_configured}',
113	        'short': f'add paths to SiteLens',
114	        'message': f'''
115	<p>To ensure accurate SiteLens reports, please
116	<a href="https://admin.webservices.umich.edu/sites/{portal_site_id}/scan-configurations/">configure at least two
117	URL paths</a>, not counting '<code>/</code>', for SiteLens to analyze on <strong>{site_name}</strong>.</p>
118	'''
119	    }, site_context)
120	
121	
122	def create_gauge_image(value: int, color: str, title: str) -> bytes:
123	    data = [value, 100 - value]
124	
125	    px = 1 / plt.rcParams['figure.dpi']  # pixel in inches
126	    fig, ax = plt.subplots(figsize=(GAUGE_PIXELS_WIDTH * px, GAUGE_PIXELS_HEIGHT * px), subplot_kw=dict(aspect="equal"))
127	
128	    ax.pie([100], radius=1.19, wedgeprops=dict(width=1.2), colors=[BACKGROUND_GAUGE_COLOR])  # solid background color inside the gauge
129	    ax.pie(data, radius=1.2, wedgeprops=dict(width=0.3), counterclock=False, startangle=90, colors=[color, 'white'])
130	
131	    plt.text(x=0, y=-0.1, s=f'{value}', horizontalalignment='center', verticalalignment='center', fontsize=20, weight='bold', color=color)
132	    ax.set_title(title, fontsize=10, weight='bold')
133	
134	    l, b, w, h = ax.get_position().bounds
135	    ax.set_position([l, b - 0.1, w, h])  # move the gauge down a bit to balance with the title
136	
137	    #plt.show()   # for tweaking or debugging
138	    #sys.exit(1)
139	
140	    buf = io.BytesIO()
141	    fig.savefig(buf, format='png')
142	    buf.seek(0)
143	    image = buf.read()
144	    buf.close()
145	    plt.close(fig)
146	    return image
147	
148	
149	def check_sitelens_scores(site_context) -> None:
150	    sc.debug('Creating section for SiteLens scores')
151	    site_name = site_context['site']['name']
152	    portal_sites = sc.config['UMich']['portal']['sites']
153	
154	    if site_name not in portal_sites:
155	        sc.console.print(f'[bold red]ERROR: Site {site_name} is not in the portal database')
156	        return
157	
158	    portal_site_id = portal_sites[site_name]['id']
159	    if portal_site_id not in sitelens_configured_scans_by_site:
160	        sc.console.print(f'[bold red]Site {site_name} has no SiteLens configurations, skipping SiteLens checks')
161	        return
162	
163	    paths = sitelens_configured_scans_by_site[portal_site_id]
164	    sc.debug(f'Checking SiteLens scores for {site_name} and paths configuration {paths}')
165	
166	    score = {
167	        'accessibility': { 'value': 0, 'label': 'Accessibility' },
168	        'performance': {'value': 0, 'label': 'Performance' },
169	        'best_practices': {'value': 0 , 'label': 'Best Practices' },
170	        'seo': {'value': 0, 'label': 'SEO' },
171	    }
172	    score_ordering = ['accessibility', 'performance', 'best_practices', 'seo']
173	
174	    scan_count = 0
175	    timestamp = datetime.datetime.min
176	    for path in paths:
177	        if path not in sitelens_scores:
178	            sc.console.print(f'[bold red]ERROR: SiteLens score for configuration {path} not found')
179	            continue
180	        scan_count += 1
181	        score['accessibility']['value'] += sitelens_scores[path]['accessibility_score']
182	        score['performance']['value'] += sitelens_scores[path]['performance_score']
183	        score['best_practices']['value'] += sitelens_scores[path]['best_practices_score']
184	        score['seo']['value'] += sitelens_scores[path]['seo_score']
185	        if sitelens_scores[path]['timestamp'] > timestamp:
186	            timestamp = sitelens_scores[path]['timestamp']
187	
188	    if scan_count == 0:
189	        sc.console.print(f'[bold red]ERROR: No SiteLens scores found for {site_name}')
190	        return
191	
192	    sitelens_date = timestamp.strftime('%Y%m%d')
193	    html = ''
194	    text = "\nSite scores:\n\n"
195	
196	    for key in score_ordering:
197	
198	        score[key]['value'] = int(round(100 * score[key]['value'] / scan_count))
199	        if score[key]['value'] >= GOOD_SCORE_MIN:
200	            color = GOOD_SCORE_COLOR
201	        elif score[key]['value'] >= OK_SCORE_MIN:
202	            color = OK_SCORE_COLOR
203	        else:
204	            color = BAD_SCORE_COLOR
205	
206	        image = create_gauge_image(score[key]['value'], color, score[key]['label'])
207	        image_cid = make_msgid(domain='webservices.umich.edu')
208	        site_context['attachments'].append({
209	            'data': image,
210	            'maintype': 'image',
211	            'subtype': 'png',
212	            'filename': f'pantheon_{site_name}_{key}_{sitelens_date}.png',
213	            'cid': image_cid,
214	            'disposition': 'inline',
215	        })
216	
217	        html += f'''
218	<td>
219	  <a href="https://admin.webservices.umich.edu/sites/{portal_site_id}/site-lens/">
220	    <img src="cid:{image_cid[1:-1]}" alt="{score[key]['label']}: {score[key]['value']} / 100"
221	      height={GAUGE_PIXELS_HEIGHT} width={GAUGE_PIXELS_WIDTH} />
222	  </a>
223	</td>
224	'''
225	
226	        text += f"{score[key]['label']:19s}: {score[key]['value']:3d} / 100\n"
227	
228	    text += "\n"
229	
230	    sc.debug(f'SiteLens scores for {site_name} at {timestamp}: A11Y={score["accessibility"]["value"]}, '
231	        f'PERF={score["performance"]["value"]}, BP={score["best_practices"]["value"]}, SEO={score["seo"]["value"]}')
232	
233	    last_run = timestamp.strftime('%B %e, %Y, %I:%M %p')
234	    text += f'as of {last_run}.\n\n'
235	
236	    site_context['sections'].append({
237	        'heading': 'SiteLens',
238	        'content': f'''
239	<table role="presentation" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="30">
240	  <tr>{html}</tr>
241	</table>
242	<p>as of {last_run}.</p>
243	
244	''',
245	        'text': text
246	    })
247
```

### ↳ Tool result

```
190	def seed_traffic(db_path, *, site_id=E2E_SITE_ID, year=2026, month=3,
191	                 plan="Performance Small"):
192	    """Seed a deterministic month of PantheonTraffic rows into a sqlite DB."""
193	    con = sqlite3.connect(str(db_path))
194	    try:
195	        day = datetime.date(year, month, 1)
196	        while day.month == month:
197	            visits = 1000 + day.day * 10
198	            con.execute(
199	                "INSERT OR REPLACE INTO pantheon_traffic "
200	                "(site_id, traffic_date, site_plan, visits, pages_served, cache_hits) "
201	                "VALUES (?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?)",
202	                (site_id, day.isoformat(), plan, visits, visits * 3, visits * 2),
203	            )
204	            day += datetime.timedelta(days=1)
205	        con.commit()
206	    finally:
207	        con.close()
208

211	    """Run the full offline shim-backed pipeline in `work`; return the CompletedProcess.
```

## Assistant

This is a key finding: the existing golden **already renders the ≤4-month "not enough data" state** ("needs 4 months more data", "available once the site has five months") — because only 2026-03 is in the report window. So:

1. P1 is conclusively not a bug (this path has always rendered), and
2. The `plan_costs` (>4-month recommendation) path is **not exercised by any e2e** — only my unit tests. That's a real gap in the refactor's end-to-end coverage.

I'll add an e2e that seeds >4 in-window months to exercise the `plan_costs` wiring, plus an explicit assertion on the existing ≤4-month state.

{
  "file_path": "/workspace/tests/e2e/test_recommendation_e2e.py",
  "content": "\"\"\"Offline e2e for the two plan-recommendation states (test-suite SPEC §7.5).\n\nThe shared rendered_report fixture has only one in-window month (June/July metrics fall after\nthe March report date), so it renders the \"not enough data yet\" state.  That already\ncharacterizes the <=4-month/new-site path (no NameError — PROBLEMS-DISCOVERED.md P1 is not a\nbug).  This module adds:\n\n  * an explicit assertion on that <=4-month state, and\n  * a >4-month run (seed six in-window months) that actually exercises the extracted plan_costs\n    cost model end to end — a path no other e2e reaches.\n\"\"\"\nimport pytest\n\nfrom conftest import (\n    E2E_DATE,\n    E2E_SITE,\n    E2E_SMTP_USERNAME,\n    MINIMAL_CONFIG,\n    make_workdir,\n    run_program,\n    seed_traffic,\n)\n\npytestmark = pytest.mark.e2e\n\n# Six consecutive in-window months ending at the March 2026 report date -> len(v) == 6 > 4.\n_SIX_MONTHS = [(2025, 10), (2025, 11), (2025, 12), (2026, 1), (2026, 2), (2026, 3)]\n\n\ndef _render(work):\n    return run_program(\n        [E2E_SITE, \"--date\", E2E_DATE, \"--smtp-username\", E2E_SMTP_USERNAME,\n         \"--config\", str(MINIMAL_CONFIG)],\n        cwd=work,\n    )\n\n\ndef test_new_site_shows_not_enough_data(rendered_report):\n    # The shared fixture (one in-window month) renders the new-site state without crashing.\n    assert rendered_report[\"proc\"].returncode == 0\n    html = rendered_report[\"html\"].read_text()\n    assert \"months more data\" in html\n    assert \"Cost estimates will be available once the site has five months\" in html\n\n\ndef test_recommendation_path_exercises_plan_costs(tmp_path):\n    work = make_workdir(tmp_path)\n    run_program([\"--create-tables\", \"--config\", str(MINIMAL_CONFIG)], cwd=work)\n    for year, month in _SIX_MONTHS:\n        seed_traffic(work / \"test.db\", year=year, month=month)\n\n    proc = _render(work)\n\n    assert proc.returncode == 0, proc.stderr\n    assert \"Traceback\" not in proc.stderr\n    html = (work / \"build\" / f\"{E2E_SITE}.html\").read_text()\n    # We are past the 5-month threshold: the recommendation table, not the \"needs data\" state.\n    assert \"months more data\" not in html\n    # plan_costs produced a cost table -> the Recommended/Current plan pills are rendered.\n    assert \"Recommended Plan\" in html\n    assert \"Current Plan\" in html\n"
}

### ↳ Tool result

```
1	#!/usr/bin/env python3
2	"""Re-record the terminus fixtures for the offline e2e/golden tier (SPEC §5.8, §8).
3	
4	Runs the program LIVE against the WordPress test site with the terminus shim in
5	`record` mode, then trims/scrubs the captured fixtures so they are safe to commit and
6	deterministic to replay:
7	  * org:site:list  -> keep only the test site (the raw call returns every org site)
8	  * domain:list    -> keep only the platform domain (drop custom domains so replay makes
9	                      no live DNS calls)
10	  * site:team:list -> replace real member emails with test-owner{N}@umich.edu
11	
12	Read-only against the test site; never uses --all/--for-real.  Run via `./run-tests --record`.
13	
14	The workdir builder, constants, and shim environment come from tests/conftest.py so there is a
15	single source of truth; recording goes through the same run_program() interlock as the tests.
16	"""
17	import json
18	import sys
19	import tempfile
20	from pathlib import Path
21	
22	# Import the harness helpers rather than re-implementing them.
23	_ROOT = Path(__file__).resolve().parents[2]
24	sys.path.insert(0, str(_ROOT / "tests"))
25	import conftest  # noqa: E402
26	
27	FIXTURES = conftest.TERMINUS_FIXTURES
28	SITE = conftest.E2E_SITE
29	DATE = conftest.E2E_DATE
30	MINIMAL_CONFIG = conftest.MINIMAL_CONFIG
31	
32	
33	def _find(argv_prefix):
34	    for fn in FIXTURES.glob("*.json"):
35	        d = json.loads(fn.read_text())
36	        if d.get("argv", [])[: len(argv_prefix)] == argv_prefix:
37	            return fn, d
38	    raise SystemExit(f"record: no captured fixture for {argv_prefix}")
39	
40	
41	def _rewrite(fn, d):
42	    fn.write_text(json.dumps(d, indent=2, ensure_ascii=False) + "\n")
43	
44	
45	def scrub():
46	    # org:site:list -> only the test site
47	    fn, d = _find(["org:site:list"])
48	    sites = json.loads(d["stdout"])
49	    kept = {sid: s for sid, s in sites.items() if s.get("name") == SITE}
50	    if len(kept) != 1:
51	        raise SystemExit(f"record: expected exactly one {SITE} in org:site:list, got {len(kept)}")
52	    d["stdout"] = json.dumps(kept)
53	    d["_scrubbed"] = "trimmed to the test site only (raw call returns all org sites)"
54	    _rewrite(fn, d)
55	
56	    # domain:list -> platform domain only (offline-safe replay)
57	    fn, d = _find(["domain:list"])
58	    dl = json.loads(d["stdout"])
59	    plat = {k: v for k, v in dl.items() if v.get("type") == "platform"}
60	    if not plat:
61	        raise SystemExit("record: no platform domain in domain:list")
62	    d["stdout"] = json.dumps(plat)
63	    d["_scrubbed"] = "custom domains removed so replay makes no live DNS calls"
64	    _rewrite(fn, d)
65	
66	    # site:team:list -> scrub emails
67	    fn, d = _find(["site:team:list"])
68	    team = json.loads(d["stdout"])
69	    scrubbed = {}
70	    for i, (mid, m) in enumerate(list(team.items())[:2]):
71	        m = dict(m)
72	        m["email"] = f"test-owner{i + 1}@umich.edu"
73	        scrubbed[mid] = m
74	    d["stdout"] = json.dumps(scrubbed)
75	    d["_scrubbed"] = "real team emails replaced with test-owner{1,2}@umich.edu"
76	    _rewrite(fn, d)
77	
78	
79	def main():
80	    FIXTURES.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
81	    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as base:
82	        work = conftest.make_workdir(base)
83	        # schema (offline), then the live recording run — both through the sanctioned
84	        # run_program interlock, with the shim in record mode.
85	        conftest.run_program(["--create-tables", "--config", MINIMAL_CONFIG], cwd=work, mode="record")
86	        print(f"record: running LIVE against {SITE} (read-only) to capture fixtures ...")
87	        proc = conftest.run_program([SITE, "--date", DATE, "--config", MINIMAL_CONFIG],
88	                                    cwd=work, mode="record")
89	        if proc.returncode != 0:
90	            sys.stderr.write(proc.stdout[-2000:] + "\n" + proc.stderr[-2000:] + "\n")
91	            raise SystemExit(f"record: live run failed (exit {proc.returncode})")
92	    scrub()
93	    n = len(list(FIXTURES.glob("*.json")))
94	    print(f"record: captured and scrubbed {n} terminus fixtures in {FIXTURES}")
95	
96	
97	if __name__ == "__main__":
98	    main()
99
```

```json
{
  "file_path": "/workspace/tests/tools/record.py",
  "content": "#!/usr/bin/env python3\n\"\"\"Re-record the terminus fixtures for the offline e2e/golden tier (SPEC §5.8, §8).\n\nRuns the program LIVE against a test site with the terminus shim in `record` mode, then\ntrims/scrubs the captured fixtures so they are safe to commit and deterministic to replay:\n  * org:site:list  -> keep only the test site (the raw call returns every org site)\n  * domain:list    -> keep only the platform domain (drop custom domains so replay makes\n                      no live DNS calls)\n  * site:team:list -> replace real member emails with test-owner{N}@umich.edu\n\nRead-only against the test site; never uses --all/--for-real.  Recording goes through the same\nrun_program() interlock as the tests.\n\nUsage (via ./run-tests --record, or directly):\n    python tests/tools/record.py            # WordPress site (its-wws-test1) -> fixtures/terminus\n    python tests/tools/record.py --drupal   # Drupal site (its-wws-test2)   -> fixtures/terminus-drupal\n\"\"\"\nimport json\nimport sys\nimport tempfile\nfrom pathlib import Path\n\n# Import the harness helpers rather than re-implementing them.\n_ROOT = Path(__file__).resolve().parents[2]\nsys.path.insert(0, str(_ROOT / \"tests\"))\nimport conftest  # noqa: E402\n\nDATE = conftest.E2E_DATE\nMINIMAL_CONFIG = conftest.MINIMAL_CONFIG\n\n\ndef _find(fixtures_dir, argv_prefix):\n    for fn in fixtures_dir.glob(\"*.json\"):\n        d = json.loads(fn.read_text())\n        if d.get(\"argv\", [])[: len(argv_prefix)] == argv_prefix:\n            return fn, d\n    raise SystemExit(f\"record: no captured fixture for {argv_prefix}\")\n\n\ndef _rewrite(fn, d):\n    fn.write_text(json.dumps(d, indent=2, ensure_ascii=False) + \"\\n\")\n\n\ndef scrub(fixtures_dir, site):\n    # org:site:list -> only the test site\n    fn, d = _find(fixtures_dir, [\"org:site:list\"])\n    sites = json.loads(d[\"stdout\"])\n    kept = {sid: s for sid, s in sites.items() if s.get(\"name\") == site}\n    if len(kept) != 1:\n        raise SystemExit(f\"record: expected exactly one {site} in org:site:list, got {len(kept)}\")\n    d[\"stdout\"] = json.dumps(kept)\n    d[\"_scrubbed\"] = \"trimmed to the test site only (raw call returns all org sites)\"\n    _rewrite(fn, d)\n\n    # domain:list -> platform domain only (offline-safe replay)\n    fn, d = _find(fixtures_dir, [\"domain:list\"])\n    dl = json.loads(d[\"stdout\"])\n    plat = {k: v for k, v in dl.items() if v.get(\"type\") == \"platform\"}\n    if not plat:\n        raise SystemExit(\"record: no platform domain in domain:list\")\n    d[\"stdout\"] = json.dumps(plat)\n    d[\"_scrubbed\"] = \"custom domains removed so replay makes no live DNS calls\"\n    _rewrite(fn, d)\n\n    # site:team:list -> scrub emails\n    fn, d = _find(fixtures_dir, [\"site:team:list\"])\n    team = json.loads(d[\"stdout\"])\n    scrubbed = {}\n    for i, (mid, m) in enumerate(list(team.items())[:2]):\n        m = dict(m)\n        m[\"email\"] = f\"test-owner{i + 1}@umich.edu\"\n        scrubbed[mid] = m\n    d[\"stdout\"] = json.dumps(scrubbed)\n    d[\"_scrubbed\"] = \"real team emails replaced with test-owner{1,2}@umich.edu\"\n    _rewrite(fn, d)\n\n\ndef record(site, fixtures_dir):\n    fixtures_dir.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as base:\n        work = conftest.make_workdir(base)\n        # schema (offline), then the live recording run — both through the sanctioned\n        # run_program interlock, with the shim in record mode.\n        conftest.run_program(\n            [\"--create-tables\", \"--config\", MINIMAL_CONFIG],\n            cwd=work, mode=\"record\", fixtures_dir=fixtures_dir,\n        )\n        print(f\"record: running LIVE against {site} (read-only) to capture fixtures ...\")\n        proc = conftest.run_program(\n            [site, \"--date\", DATE, \"--config\", MINIMAL_CONFIG],\n            cwd=work, mode=\"record\", fixtures_dir=fixtures_dir,\n        )\n        if proc.returncode != 0:\n            sys.stderr.write(proc.stdout[-2000:] + \"\\n\" + proc.stderr[-2000:] + \"\\n\")\n            raise SystemExit(f\"record: live run failed (exit {proc.returncode})\")\n    scrub(fixtures_dir, site)\n    n = len(list(fixtures_dir.glob(\"*.json\")))\n    print(f\"record: captured and scrubbed {n} terminus fixtures in {fixtures_dir}\")\n\n\ndef main():\n    if \"--drupal\" in sys.argv[1:]:\n        record(conftest.E2E_SITE2, conftest.TERMINUS_FIXTURES_DRUPAL)\n    else:\n        record(conftest.E2E_SITE, conftest.TERMINUS_FIXTURES)\n\n\nif __name__ == \"__main__\":\n    main()\n"
}
```

### ⚙ Tool call: `Read`

```json
{
  "file_path": "/workspace/tests/render/test_render.py"
}
```

### ↳ Tool result

```
1	"""Render tier: load the report HTML in a headless browser and check it renders (SPEC §9).
2	
3	The report's images are attached by Content-ID (cid:), which a standalone browser can't
4	resolve, so we extract them from the .eml, write them locally, rewrite the cid: refs, then
5	load the page and assert the DOM structure and that the banner image actually resolves.
6	
7	If Chromium can't launch (its browser binary or system libraries aren't installed), the
8	test SKIPS with the exact setup command rather than erroring — the render logic is fine,
9	the environment just needs a one-time provisioning step.
10	"""
11	import email
12	import re
13	
14	import pytest
15	
16	pytestmark = pytest.mark.render
17	
18	_CID_REF = re.compile(r"cid:([^\"'\s>]+)")
19	_SETUP_HINT = "one-time setup: python -m playwright install --with-deps chromium"
20	
21	
22	def _rewrite_cids_to_local(rendered_report, dest_dir):
23	    """Extract inline images from the .eml and rewrite the HTML's cid: refs to file URIs."""
24	    msg = email.message_from_bytes(rendered_report["eml"].read_bytes())
25	    cid_to_uri = {}
26	    for part in msg.walk():
27	        cid = part.get("Content-ID")
28	        if cid and part.get_content_maintype() == "image":
29	            key = cid.strip("<>")
30	            out = dest_dir / f"{key}.{part.get_content_subtype()}"
31	            out.write_bytes(part.get_payload(decode=True))
32	            cid_to_uri[key] = out.as_uri()
33	    html = rendered_report["html"].read_text()
34	    html = _CID_REF.sub(lambda m: cid_to_uri.get(m.group(1), m.group(0)), html)
35	    page_file = dest_dir / "render.html"
36	    page_file.write_text(html)
37	    return page_file
38	
39	
40	def test_report_renders_in_browser(rendered_report, tmp_path):
41	    from playwright.sync_api import sync_playwright
42	
43	    page_file = _rewrite_cids_to_local(rendered_report, tmp_path)
44	
45	    pw = sync_playwright().start()
46	    try:
47	        try:
48	            browser = pw.chromium.launch()
49	        except Exception as exc:  # noqa: BLE001 - environment provisioning, not a test failure
50	            pytest.skip(f"Chromium can't launch ({type(exc).__name__}); {_SETUP_HINT}")
51	        try:
52	            page = browser.new_page()
53	            page.goto(page_file.as_uri())
54	            assert "Pantheon Traffic Report" in page.title()
55	            assert page.locator("img.banner_image").count() == 1
56	            # The banner image resolved to real pixels (cid rewrite worked, asset loaded).
57	            banner_width = page.eval_on_selector("img.banner_image", "el => el.naturalWidth")
58	            assert banner_width and banner_width > 0
59	        finally:
60	            browser.close()
61	    finally:
62	        pw.stop()
63
```

### ⚙ Tool call: `Write`

```json
{
  "file_path": "/workspace/tests/render/test_render.py",

accessibility violations outside a small, explicit allowlist.\n\nIf Chromium can't launch (browser binary or system libraries not installed), the test SKIPS\nwith the exact setup command rather than for this tool.\n#   * region / landmark-*: email HTML has no ARIA landmarks by design.\n_AXE_ALLOWLIST = {\"color-contrast\", \"region\"}\n\n\ndef _rewrite_cids_to_local(rendered, dest_dir):\n    \"\"\"Extract inline images from the .eml and rewrite the HTML's cid: refs to file URIs.\"\"\"\n    msg = email.message_from_bytes(rendered[\"eml\"].read_bytes())\n    cid_to_uri = {}\n    for part in    try:\n        try:\n            browser = pw.chromium.launch()\n        except Exception as exc:  # noqa: BLE001 - environment provisioning, not a test failure\n            pytest.skip(f\"Chromium can't launch ({type(exc).__name__}); {_SETUP_HINT}\")\n        try:\n            page = browser.new_page()\n            console_errors = []\n            page.on(\"console\", lambda m: console_errors.append(m.text) if m.type == \"error\" else None)\n            page.goto(page_file.as_uri(), wait_until=\"load\")\n\n            # ── structure ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n            assert \"Pantheon Traffic Report\" in page.title()\n            assert page.locator(\"img.banner_image\").count() == 1\n            assert page.locator(\"img.chart_image\").count() >= 1\n            banner_width = page.eval_on_selector(\"img.banner_image\", \"el => el.naturalWidth\")\n            assert banner_width and banner_width > 0  # banner actually loaded\n\n            # ── no console errors (email HTML has no JS; broken assets would show here) ─\n            assert console_errors == [], f\"console errors: {console_errors}\"\n\n            # ── accessibility smoke (axe-core, vendored; offline) ─────────────────────\n            page.add_script_tag(path=str(_AXE))\n            result = page.evaluate(\"async () => await axe.run(document)\")\n            serious = [\n                v for v in result[\"violations\"]\n                if v.get(\"impact\") in (\"serious\", \"critical\") and v[\"id\"] not in _AXE_ALLOWLIST\n            ]\n            assert not serious, \"axe serious/critical violations: \" + json.dumps(\n                [(v[\"id\"], v[\"impact\"]) for v in serious]\n            )\n        finally:\n            browser.close()\n    finally:\n        pw.stop()\n"
}

1	# Problems discovered while designing the test suite
2	
3	Logged during the 2026-07-04 test-suite **design** session (see `PROMPT.md` / `SPEC.md` in this
4	folder). Per the driving prompt, program bugs are **logged here and fixed in a later session**,
5	**with one exception**: the single *blocking* bug (P1 below) is fixed as part of test-suite
6	implementation because it makes a valid, common program state (a new site with ≤4 months of
7	traffic) untestable.
8	
9	Line numbers refer to the working revision at design time (`pantheon-sitehealth-emails`, ~3702
10	lines). They will drift; treat them as starting points and re-locate by the described symptom.
11	
12	All problems below were found by **reading** the code (plus targeted verification reads). None
13	were reproduced by *running* the program against real sites, because the safety constraints
14	forbid `--all` / `--for-real` / live `--create-tables` / live `--import-older-metrics`. Each
15	entry notes what still needs to be confirmed at fix time.
16	
17	---
18	
19	## P1 — BLOCKING (fixed during test-suite implementation): `NameError` rendering a site with ≤4 months of traffic
20	
21	**Symptom.** For any site whose traffic history is ≤4 months, `main()` raises
22	`NameError: name 'median_visitors' is not defined` (and, on related paths,
23	`site_current_plan_index` / `site_recommended_plan_index`) while assembling `template_dict`.
24	
25	**Root cause.**
26	- `median_visitors` is assigned only inside `if len(v) > 4:` at **L3155**.
27	- `site_current_plan_index` / `site_recommended_plan_index` are assigned even deeper — inside
28	  `if len(v) > 4:` **and** the nested `if site["plan_name"] != site_recommended_plan:` branch
29	  (**L3177–3179**).
30	- But `template_dict` consumes all three **unconditionally**: `median_monthly_visitors=f"{median_visitors:,.0f}"`
31	  at **L3555**, and the two indices at **L3544–3545**. This dict is built in Python *before*
32	  Jinja sees it, so no template `{% if %}` guard can prevent the `NameError`.
33	
34	**Why it hasn't blown up in production / existing tests.** The one existing golden
35	(`its-wws-test1`) replays recorded metrics that supply >4 months of history, so `len(v) > 4`
36	and the variables are defined. Real U-M sites are almost all long-lived. A brand-new site (or
37	any site with a short history) hits this. It is also latent cross-iteration state: under `--all`
38	a prior site's `median_visitors` can leak into a later ≤4-month site, masking the bug
39	non-deterministically.
40	
41	**Fix (folded into the `recommend_plan(...)` extraction — see SPEC Part A/B).** Have
42	`recommend_plan` always return a complete result dict, including for the ≤4-month case:
43	`median_visitors = 0` (or mean of available months), `current_plan_index` /
44	`recommended_plan_index` defaulting to the current plan's index, empty `cost_table_rows`,
45	`months_until_recommendations = 5 - len(v)`. `main()` reads these off the returned dict so
46	`template_dict` is always well-defined.
47	
48	**Verify at fix time.** Offline e2e with `its-wws-test1` seeded with ≤4 months of traffic renders
49	without error and the template shows the "not enough data yet" state; the >4-month golden stays
50	byte-identical (modulo intended output for the new-site case).
51	
52	---
```

With no traffic, `plan_on_day` is empty and `days[0]` raises\n`IndexError: list index out of range`.\n\n**How it surfaced.** Recording Drupal fixtures against `its-wws-test2` (a fresh site with no\nlive traffic) crashed here until the recording flow was changed to **seed a month of traffic\nbefore the live run** (`tests/tools/record.py`). The harness already sidesteps this in the\noffline e2e by seeding traffic (see the `seed_traffic` note in `conftest.py`).\n\n**Fix later.** Guard the aggregation: if `plan_on_day` is empty, emit a notice / skip the plan\nsections gracefully rather than indexing `days[0]`. This is the same class of \"a genuinely new\nsite\" robustness gap as P1's (non-)issue, but here it is a real crash.\n\n**Verify at fix time.** A site (or seeded DB) with zero in-window traffic renders a report (or a\nclean \"no traffic yet\" message) instead of raising `IndexError`.\n\n---\n\n## Non-issues considered and dismissed"
}

```
=== README Testing section ===
## Testing

The project has a pytest-based test harness under `tests/`.  See
[`tests/README.md`](tests/README.md) for the full layout and how to add tests.

Install the test dependencies (once), plus the headless browser used by the render tier:

```bash
uv pip install .[test]
python -m playwright install --with-deps chromium   # needs sudo for the system libraries
```

Run the tests with the `./run-tests` wrapper (a thin front-end for pytest):

```bash
./run-tests              # everything, including the live tier (needs Terminus auth + network)
./run-tests --fast       # offline subset only: unit + integration + shim e2e + golden + render
./run-tests --llm        # terse, machine-parseable summary (for pasting failures into an assistant)
./run-tests --coverage   # report coverage (no gate; in-process tiers only)
./run-tests --update-goldens   # refresh the rendered-report snapshots after an intended change
./run-tests --record     # re-record the terminus fixtures from the live test site (read-only)
```

Any other arguments (`-k EXPR`, `-m MARK`, file paths) are passed straight through to pytest,
e.g. `./run-tests -m "e2e"` or `./run-tests tests/unit`.

Tiers are selected by pytest marks: `unit`, `integration`, `e2e`, `live`, `render`, `email`,
`slow`.  `--fast` excludes `live` and `slow`.  The `email` tier is a deferred, skipped scaffold
(it activates when email sending is re-enabled).  Two hard rules the harness enforces: tests
never run the program with `--all` or `--for-real` (a `run_program()` interlock refuses them),
and they use only the `its-wws-test1` / `its-wws-test2` test sites, read-only.

## TO DO

* update CLAUDE.md again (prompt)
* add SendGrid support as an additional option to SMTP
  * Make sure Claude can use Chrome / headless chrome as installed in the container, together with Chrome DevTools Integration
  * Implement SMTP testing, GMail testing (see test harness prompt for requirements)
* fqdns.json (get direct from Cloudflare instead; refresh if --all or multiple sites and >= 24h)
* add cf-cache-status, cache-control checks
=== CLAUDE.md Testing section ===
## Testing

There is a pytest harness under `tests/` (built 2026-07; design in
`development/2026-07-04-test-harness/SPEC.md`). Run it with `./run-tests` (wrapper over
pytest): `./run-tests --fast` is the offline inner loop; `./run-tests` adds the live tier;
`--llm` gives terse machine-parseable output; `--coverage`, `--update-goldens`, and
`--record` do what they say. Tiers are pytest marks: `unit`, `integration`, `e2e`, `live`,
`render`, `email`, `slow`. **When you change the program, add/adjust the appropriate tests in
the same change** (this project does not do TDD — tests follow the change).

Non-obvious things the harness relies on:
- **The script is imported, not re-parsed.** `tests/conftest.py` loads the extension-less
  `pantheon-sitehealth-emails` via `importlib`/`SourceFileLoader` (fixture `psh`). Argparse was
  refactored into `build_arg_parser()`/`parse_args()`; `sc.options` is set by the caller, so a
  test sets it (the `reset_sc` autouse fixture does) before calling functions. `MPLBACKEND=Agg`
  must be set before the load (conftest does this) because the module imports `matplotlib.pyplot`
  at the top.
- **Two mock seams.** All Pantheon/WP/Drush I/O funnels through `run_terminus()` — monkeypatch it
  for in-process tests, or use the PATH-shim fake `terminus` (`tests/shims/terminus`, record/replay)
  for full subprocess e2e. The `php inline-styles.php` CSS inliner uses **real php**.
- **Safety interlock.** `run_program()` in conftest is the only sanctioned way to run the program
  in a subprocess; it raises `ForbiddenFlagError` if `--all`/`-a`/`--for-real` appear. Never
  bypass it. Tests use only `its-wws-test1`/`its-wws-test2`, read-only.
- **Offline e2e determinism.** The shim-backed run uses `tests/fixtures/config/minimal.toml`,
  seeded traffic, `--date 2026-03-31` (a mid-year date avoids the U-M contract-year-end path),
  and a `domain:list` fixture reduced to the platform domain (so no live DNS). Golden snapshots
  normalize the volatile `make_msgid` CIDs; refresh with `./run-tests --update-goldens`. Refresh
  terminus fixtures with `./run-tests --record` (trims org list to the test site, scrubs emails).
- **The reusable (non-UMich) path had latent bugs** that production never hit because U-M always
  runs with the UMich plugin enabled. Several U-M-specific code paths in the core script are not
  yet behind the `[UMich].enabled` flag; the planned refactor should move them out. When adding
  code, keep institution-specific logic behind config flags / the `umich` plugin+check packages.

## Development archive (`development/`)
```

### ↳ Tool result

```
1	# Test harness for `pantheon-sitehealth-emails`
2	
3	Design and rationale: [`../development/2026-07-04-test-harness/SPEC.md`](../development/2026-07-04-test-harness/SPEC.md).
4	This README is the practical, day-to-day reference.
5	
6	## Running
7	
8	Use the `./run-tests` wrapper (from the repo root):
9	
10	| Command | What it does |
11	|---|---|
12	| `./run-tests` | All tiers, including `live` (needs Terminus auth + network). |
13	| `./run-tests --fast` | Offline subset: `-m "not live and not slow"`. The inner loop. |
14	| `./run-tests --llm` | Terse, machine-parseable summary (`LLM_SUMMARY …` + `FAILED <nodeid>`). |
15	| `./run-tests --coverage` | Report coverage (no gate; **in-process tiers only**, see below). |
16	| `./run-tests --update-goldens` | Refresh the rendered-report snapshots after an intended change. |
17	| `./run-tests --record` | Re-record the terminus fixtures from the live test site (read-only). |
18	
19	Extra args pass through to pytest: `./run-tests -m e2e`, `./run-tests -k drush`, `./run-tests tests/unit`.
20	
21	First-time setup:
22	
23	```bash
24	uv pip install .[test]
25	python -m playwright install --with-deps chromium   # render tier; --with-deps needs sudo
26	```
27	
28	If Chromium isn't installed, the `render` test **skips** with the exact setup command (it does
29	not fail).
30	
31	## Layout
32	
33	```
34	tests/
35	  conftest.py        # fixtures + the run_program() safety interlock (start here)
36	  fixtures/
37	    config/          # minimal.toml (plugins off) + full.toml (plugins on); self-contained
38	    terminus/        # recorded terminus responses, keyed by a hash of the argv
39	  shims/terminus     # fake terminus (record/replay) put on PATH for e2e
40	  tools/record.py    # re-records + trims/scrubs the terminus fixtures
41	  __snapshots__/     # syrupy golden baselines (normalized rendered report)
42	  unit/              # pure/in-process helpers + Hypothesis + the interlock test
43	  integration/       # monkeypatched run_terminus, temp DB, check hooks, bug regressions
44	  e2e/               # full subprocess run via the shim; artifact + golden assertions
45	  live/              # real terminus, read-only (marked live+slow)
46	  render/            # headless-browser render of the report
47	  email/             # deferred GMail round-trip scaffold (skipped)
48	```
49	
50	## Marks / tiers
51	
52	`unit`, `integration`, `e2e`, `live`, `render`, `email`, `slow`. `--fast` excludes `live` and
53	`slow`. Choose the relevant subset for a change (e.g. a Drupal-check edit → `-m "unit or integration" -k drush`
54	plus the Drupal live/e2e cases).
55	
56	## Writing a test
57	
58	- Get the program module from the `psh` fixture (it's imported once; don't import it yourself).
59	- `sc.options` is pre-set by the autouse `reset_sc` fixture (which also isolates `sc` global
60	  state between tests). Request `reset_sc` if you need the `sc` module object.
61	- For in-process Pantheon calls, `monkeypatch.setattr(psh, "run_terminus", fake)`.
62	- To run the whole program, use the `program_runner` fixture (or the module-scoped
63	  `rendered_report` fixture, which runs the offline pipeline once and exposes the artifacts).
64	  **Never** invoke the program except through `run_program` — it enforces the `--all`/`--for-real`
65	  interlock.
66	- Temp DB: the `temp_db` fixture gives a fresh sqlite engine + session + the ORM models.
67	
68	## Determinism notes
69	
70	- The offline e2e uses `minimal.toml`, seeded traffic, and `--date 2026-03-31` (mid-year, to
71	  avoid the U-M contract-year-end code path). The `domain:list` fixture is reduced to the platform
72	  domain so replay makes **no live DNS** calls.
73	- Golden snapshots normalize the volatile `make_msgid` CIDs (`cid:…` → `cid:NORMALIZED`). The
74	  matplotlib chart/gauge PNGs are attached by CID and not byte-compared. `MPLBACKEND=Agg` is
75	  forced before the module loads.
76	- Regenerate golden snapshots only deliberately: `./run-tests --update-goldens`, then review the diff.
77	
78	## Recording / refreshing terminus fixtures
79	
80	`./run-tests --record` runs the program live against `its-wws-test1` (read-only) with the shim in
81	record mode, then trims `org:site:list` to the test site, reduces `domain:list` to the platform
82	domain, and scrubs `site:team:list` emails to `test-owner{1,2}@umich.edu`. Review the diff before
83	committing; each fixture carries a `recorded` date.
84	
85	## Coverage
86	
87	`--coverage` measures the **in-process** tiers (unit/integration). The e2e/live tiers run the
88	program in a subprocess that pytest-cov does not see unless `COVERAGE_PROCESS_START` +
89	`coverage.process_startup()` plumbing is added (not wired yet). So the reported number reflects
90	in-process code, not whole-program coverage. There is no coverage gate by design.
91
```

## What was built

**Refactor (Part A) — behavior-preserving, WordPress golden byte-identical (0-line diff):**
Extracted four pure, importable helpers from `main()` — `overage_blocks`, `contract_year_end`, `estimate_month_visits`, and `plan_costs` (the cost model, DB-free via an injected `op_lookup`). Removed the `overage_blocks` name-shadow the review flagged. Per your decision, the U-M downgrade guardrails/notices stayed in `main()` for the later de-monolith stage.

**Interlock hardening (Part C):** `run_program` now raises `ForbiddenLiveDataError` if `--create-tables`/`--import-older-metrics` would run live or against a non-fixture config — a realpath **allowlist**, not a backend-type check (the fail-open the review caught).

**~17 new test files** — unit (plan math, `plan_costs`, config-substitution, argparse, property), integration (wrappers, DB, MIME CID-integrity), mock-based plugin/check tests (AWS, Cloudflare, umich-portal via temp SQLite, SiteLens), a Drupal golden, a recommendation e2e, and a reworked render tier (console-error + vendored axe-core a11y smoke, both reports).

**Drupal path:** recorded `its-wws-test2` (drush) into a **separate** `tests/fixtures/terminus-drupal/` (WordPress fixtures untouched), with a second golden.

## Three things that changed from the approved spec (all in SPEC §14 / PROBLEMS-DISCOVERED)

1. **P1 was not a bug.** The ≤4-month `NameError` doesn't happen — the variables are initialized at L985–988/L3097, which my design-time check missed. No code fix. The offline golden already renders that state; I added an explicit assertion plus a >4-month e2e that seeds traffic to exercise `plan_costs` end-to-end (a path the golden never reaches).
2. **`recommend_plan` → `plan_costs`** (you chose this): the full block was too entangled with U-M messaging to extract cleanly.
3. **Two new bugs found by running the code** (logged, not fixed): **P9** — a real `link-name` a11y defect in the template (allowlisted in the render smoke so it still catches *new* issues); **P10** — `IndexError` on a zero-traffic site (worked around in the recorder by seeding).

## User

<command-message>code-review</command-message>
<command-name>/code-review</command-name>
<command-args>high</command-args>

## User

`high effort → 3+5 angles × 6 candidates → 1-vote verify (recall-biased) → ≤10 findings`

You are reviewing for **recall** at high effort: catch every real bug a careful
reviewer would catch in one sitting. At this level, catching real bugs matters
more than avoiding false positives. Err on the side of surfacing.

## Phase 0 — Gather the diff

Run `git diff @{upstream}...HEAD` (or `git diff main...HEAD` / `git diff HEAD~1`
if there's no upstream) to get the unified diff under review. If there are
uncommitted changes, or the range diff is empty, also run `git diff HEAD` and
include the working-tree changes in scope — the review often runs before the
commit. If a PR number, branch name, or file path was passed as an argument,
review that target instead. Treat this diff as the review scope.

## Phase 1 — Find candidates (3 correctness angles + 3 cleanup angles + 1 altitude angle + 1 conventions angle, up to 6 each)

Run **8 independent finder angles** via the Agent tool. Each
surfaces **up to 6 candidate findings** with `file`, `line`, a one-line
`summary`, and a concrete `failure_scenario`.

### Angle A — line-by-line diff scan

Read every hunk in the diff, line by line. Then Read the enclosing function for
each hunk — bugs in unchanged lines of a touched function are in scope (the PR
re-exposes or fails to fix them). For every line ask: what input, state, timing,
or platform makes this line wrong? Look for inverted/wrong conditions,
off-by-one, null/undefined deref, missing `await`, falsy-zero checks,
wrong-variable copy-paste, error swallowed in catch, unescaped regex metachars.

### Angle B — removed-behavior auditor

For every line the diff DELETES or replaces, name the invariant or behavior it
enforced, then search the new code for where that invariant is re-established.
If you can't find it, that's a candidate: a removed guard, a dropped error
path, a narrowed validation, a deleted test that was covering a real case.

### Angle C — cross-file tracer

For each function the diff changes, find its callers (Grep for the symbol) and
check whether the change breaks any call site: a new precondition, a changed
return shape, a new exception, a timing/ordering dependency. Also check callees:
does a parallel change in the same PR make a call unsafe?

### Reuse

The angles above hunt for bugs; this one and the next two hunt for cleanup in
the changed code. Flag new code that re-implements something the codebase
already has — Grep shared/utility modules and files adjacent to the change,
and name the existing helper to call instead.

### Simplification

Flag unnecessary complexity the diff adds: redundant or derivable state,
copy-paste with slight variation, deep nesting, dead code left behind. Name
the simpler form that does the same job.

### Efficiency

Flag wasted work the diff introduces: redundant computation or repeated I/O,
independent operations run sequentially, blocking work added to startup or
hot paths. Also flag long-lived objects built from closures or captured
environments — they keep the entire enclosing scope alive for the object's
lifetime (a memory leak when that scope holds large values); prefer a
class/struct that copies only the fields it needs. Name the cheaper
alternative.

### Altitude

Check that each change is implemented at the right depth, not as a fragile
bandaid. Special cases layered on shared infrastructure are a sign the fix
isn't deep enough — prefer generalizing the underlying mechanism over adding
special cases.

### Conventions (CLAUDE.md)

Find the CLAUDE.md files that govern the changed code: the user-level
~/.claude/CLAUDE.md, the repo-root CLAUDE.md, plus any CLAUDE.md or
CLAUDE.local.md in a directory that is an ancestor of a changed file (a
directory's CLAUDE.md only applies to files at or below it). Read each one
that exists, then check the diff for clear violations of the rules they state.

Only flag a violation when you can quote the exact rule and the exact line
that breaks it — no style preferences, no vague "spirit of the doc"
inferences. In the finding, name the CLAUDE.md path and quote the rule so the
report can cite it. If no CLAUDE.md applies, return nothing for this angle.

Cleanup, altitude, and conventions candidates use the same
`file`/`line`/`summary` shape; in `failure_scenario`, state the concrete
cost (what is duplicated, wasted, harder to maintain, or which CLAUDE.md rule
is broken) instead of a crash. Correctness bugs always outrank cleanup,
altitude, and conventions findings when the output cap forces a cut.

Pass every candidate with a nameable failure scenario through — finders that
silently drop half-believed candidates bypass the verify step and are the
dominant cause of misses.

## Phase 2 — Verify (1-vote, recall-biased)

Dedup near-duplicates (same defect, same location, same reason → keep one). For
each remaining candidate, run **one verifier** via the Agent tool:
give it the diff, the relevant file(s), and the candidate; it returns exactly
one of **CONFIRMED / PLAUSIBLE / REFUTED**.

**PLAUSIBLE by default** — do not refute a candidate for being "speculative" or
"depends on runtime state" when the state is realistic: concurrency races,
nil/undefined on a rare-but-reachable path (error handler, cold cache, missing
optional field), falsy-zero treated as missing, off-by-one on a boundary the
code does not exclude, retry storms / partial failures, regex/allowlist that
lost an anchor. These are PLAUSIBLE.

**REFUTED** only when constructible from the code: factually wrong (quote the
actual line); provably impossible (type/constant/invariant — show it); already
handled in this diff (cite the guard); or pure style with no observable effect.

Keep **CONFIRMED and PLAUSIBLE**. Drop REFUTED.

## Output

Return findings as a JSON array of at most 10 objects:

```json
[
  {
    "file": "path/to/file.ext",
    "line": 123,
    "summary": "one-sentence statement of the bug",
    "failure_scenario": "concrete inputs/state → wrong output/crash"
  }
]
```

Ranked most-severe first. If more than 10 survive, keep the 10 most
severe. If nothing survives verification, return `[]`.

+def overage_blocks(overage, overage_block_size) -> int:
+    """Number of overage blocks billed for `overage` visits (rounded to the nearest block)."""
+    return round((overage + overage_block_size / 2.0) / overage_block_size)
+
+
+def contract_year_end(report_date: datetime.date) -> bool:
+    """True if `report_date` is in the U-M contract-year-end window (June 16-29)."""
+    return report_date.month == 6 and 16 <= report_date.day < 30
+
+
+def estimate_month_visits(visits_by_month, dates, last_day, end_day) -> int:
+    """Extrapolate the final (partial) month's visits.
+
+    Returns -1 when the reporting month is complete or too early to extrapolate (i.e. not
+    ``1 < end_day < last_day``), matching the inline behavior it replaces.  ``dates`` is the
+    ordered list of month midpoints (datetime.date) whose keys index ``visits_by_month``.
+    """
+    estimate = -1
+    if last_day > end_day > 1:
+        extrapolate = (
+            visits_by_month[dates[-1].strftime("%Y-%m")] * last_day / (end_day - 1)
+        )
+        if len(visits_by_month) > 1:
+            previous_month = visits_by_month[dates[-2].strftime("%Y-%m")]
+            if last_day >= 25:
+                estimate = round(extrapolate)
+            elif last_day >= 15:
+                estimate = round((2 * extrapolate + previous_month) / 3)
+            else:
+                estimate = round((extrapolate + previous_month) / 2)
+        else:
+            estimate = round(extrapolate)
+    return estimate
+
+
+def plan_costs(
+    plan_info,
+    plan_names,
+    visits_by_month,
+    v,
+    estimate,
+    end_date_yyyy_mm,
+    site_plan_start,
+    overage_block_size,
+    overage_block_cost,
+    op_lookup,
+):
+    """Project each plan's annual cost for a site and pick per-plan cost metrics.
+
+    Pure cost model extracted from main().  ``op_lookup(month) -> PantheonOverageProtection
+    | None`` injects the overage-protection state so this function does no DB I/O.  Returns
+    ``(cost_same, costs_median, costs_best, median_visitors)``.  Only invoked when a site has
+    more than four months of data (main() leaves ``median_visitors = 0`` otherwise).
+    """
+    sc.debug("[bold magenta]=== Generating plan recommendations:")
+    sc.debug("===== future costs for same traffic")
+    cost_same = {}
+    costs_median = {}
+    for plan in plan_names:
+        cost = float(plan_info[plan]["cost"])
+        cost_by_month = []
+        cost_for_plan_months = []
+        op_remaining = 0
+        for month in visits_by_month.keys():
+            visits = visits_by_month[month]
+            if month == end_date_yyyy_mm and estimate > 0:
+                visits = estimate
+            overage = max(visits - int(plan_info[plan]["traffic_limit"]), 0)
+            overage_cost = overage_blocks(overage, overage_block_size) * overage_block_cost
+            if plan != "Basic":
+                op = op_lookup(month)
+                if op is not None:
+                    if op.used_this_month:
+                        overage_cost = 0
+                else:
+                    if month.endswith("-01"):
+                        op_remaining = 4
+                    if overage > 0 and op_remaining > 0:
+                        overage_cost = 0
+                        op_remaining -= 1
+            cost += overage_cost
+            cost_by_month.append(overage_cost)
+            if month >= site_plan_start.strftime("%Y-%m"):
+                cost_for_plan_months.append(overage_cost)
+        if len(cost_by_month) < 12:
+            cost += (12 - len(cost_by_month)) * np.median(cost_for_plan_months)
+        cost_same[plan] = cost
+        sc.debug(f"{plan}: ${cost:,.2f}")
+
+    v = list(v)
+    if estimate > 0:
+        v[-1] = estimate
+    median_visitors = np.median(v)
+    sc.debug(f"Median Pantheon visitors per month: {median_visitors:,.0f}")
+    sc.debug("===== future costs for median traffic")
+    for plan in plan_names:
+        overage = median_visitors - int(plan_info[plan]["traffic_limit"])
+        if overage < 0:
+            overage = 0
+        months_without_op = 12 if plan == "Basic" else 8
+        costs_median[plan] = (
+            float(plan_info[plan]["cost"])
+            + overage_blocks(overage, overage_block_size)
+            * overage_block_cost
+            * months_without_op
+        )
+        sc.debug(f"{plan}: ${costs_median[plan]:,.2f}")
+
+    # find best costs
+    # For each plan, we want to be conservative by picking the highest cost metric:
+    costs_best = {p: max(cost_same[p], costs_median[p]) for p in plan_names}
+    return cost_same, costs_median, costs_best, median_visitors
+

## Adversarial review: `tests/conftest.py` + `tests/tools/record.py`

1. **conftest.py:342-380 (`_assert_offline_data_flags` + `_resolve_config_arg`) — CRITICAL fail-open via `--` asymmetry.** The dangerous-flag scan stops at `--` (line 351), but `_resolve_config_arg` scans the *entire* arg list and never stops at `--`. This makes the guard's notion of the "effective config" disagree with argparse. Failure scenario (verified against argparse): `run_program(["--create-tables", "--", "--config", str(CONFIG_DIR/"minimal.toml")], cwd=work)`. argparse activates `--create-tables` (before `--`) but treats `--config minimal.toml` as *positionals*, so the program uses its **default (production) config/DB**. Meanwhile `_resolve_config_arg` picks up the post-`--` `--config` value, resolves it under the allowlist, and the guard PASSES — letting `--create-tables` run against the production database. The guard fails open on exactly the property it exists to protect (C2).

2. **conftest.py:364 (`mode == "live"` branch) — live-mode refusal does not cover the real live path.** The terminus shim only understands `"record"` and `"replay"` (tests/shims/terminus:52-55); `mode="live"` is used *only* by `test_interlock.py:51` to exercise the guard. The genuine live-against-Pantheon path is `record.py`, which runs `--create-tables` and the capture with `mode="record"` — which is NOT `"live"`, so it skips the live refusal entirely and relies solely on the config-path allowlist. Failure scenario: a future/edited live recording invoked with `mode="record"` and a production config would sail past the `mode=="live"` guard; only the path allowlist stands between it and the production DB. The safety branch is keyed to a mode string the real live path never uses.

3. **conftest.py:398 (`fixtures_dir or TERMINUS_FIXTURES`) — empty Path is truthy, defeating the fallback.** Verified: `Path("")` is `PosixPath('.')` and is truthy, so `Path("") or TERMINUS_FIXTURES` yields `.`, not the fallback. Failure scenario: a caller passing `fixtures_dir=Path("")` (e.g. from an unset/blank config value coerced to Path) silently sets `TERMINUS_SHIM_DIR="."` instead of the WordPress fixtures, causing replay to find no fixtures. No current caller does this (callers pass `None` or a real dir), so low severity — but the `or` idiom is unsafe for Path and would not do what it reads as.

4. **conftest.py:329-333 (`_resolve_config_arg`) — glued short option `-cX` unrecognized (resolver/argparse divergence).** The resolver handles `--config X`, `--config=X`, `-c X`, `-c=X`, but NOT the glued `-cFOO` form, which argparse accepts as `config=FOO` (verified). Failure scenario: `run_program(["--create-tables", "-c"+str(CONFIG_DIR/"minimal.toml")], ...)` → resolver returns `None` → guard refuses a legitimate, properly-allowlisted run. This direction is fail-*closed* (safe but breaks a valid invocation). It is the benign twin of finding #1: the resolver's arg model diverges from argparse's, and only the `--` split turns that divergence fail-open.

5. **conftest.py:184 + record.py:78-96 — drupal render/record depends on `E2E_SITE2_ID` exactly matching the ID the program derives for `its-wws-test2`.** `seed_traffic` keys rows on the passed `site_id` (line 208), but the report aggregation looks up traffic by the site ID the program obtains from the terminus `site:info` fixture. If the hardcoded `E2E_SITE2_ID = "acb22aef-..."` does not equal that derived ID, the seeded rows are unreachable and the aggregation still `IndexError`s — i.e. the new seed-before-record step only prevents the crash the comment claims when the constant is exactly right. I could not verify the literal against live Pantheon; note it is self-checking only at record time (a wrong ID makes the live record run fail loudly), but a stale/typo'd constant silently reintroduces the empty-traffic IndexError.

6. **record.py:98-101 (`--drupal` dispatch) — `"--drupal" in sys.argv[1:]` is correct but positional-fragile.** Detection works when invoked as `python tests/tools/record.py --drupal` or forwarded by `run-tests`. The only nameable failure: because it is a substring-membership test rather than argparse, an unrelated future arg or a value like `--drupal=1` would not match (`--drupal=1 != --drupal`), silently recording the WordPress site into `fixtures/terminus` instead. Minor, but worth pinning if `run-tests` ever forwards flags with values. Arg order in `record(site, site_id, fixtures_dir)` and both `main()` call sites is correct (verified: `record(E2E_SITE2, E2E_SITE2_ID, TERMINUS_FIXTURES_DRUPAL)` matches the signature).

**Bottom line:** Finding #1 is the real safety bug — a constructible `--`-based invocation makes the extended interlock fail open and run `--create-tables` against the production config/DB. Findings #2 (mode="live" not covering the actual live path) and #5 (drupal ID coupling) are the next most consequential.</result>

## Verdict: no correctness-changing divergence found

I could not construct a nameable failure scenario for any of the four functions. Below is what I verified for each of the hunt items, including the two that looked riskiest.

**1. `estimate_month_visits` guard rewrite — VERIFIED EQUIVALENT (no bug).**
`/workspace/pantheon-sitehealth-emails:2729-2730`. The new `if estimate != -1:` gate is exactly equivalent to the original `if last_day &gt; end_date.day &gt; 1:`. Inside the original block, `estimate` is unconditionally reassigned via `round(...)` on non-negative quantities (visits ≥ 0, `last_day/(end_day-1) &gt; 0`), so it is always ≥ 0 there and stays `-1` otherwise. Since `estimate` is always an int in `{-1} ∪ [0,∞)`, `estimate != -1` ⟺ `estimate &gt;= 0` ⟺ the original condition. The downstream chart consumers (`if estimate &gt;= 0:` at L2774 and the render kwarg at L3606-3607) therefore see `estimates` defined in exactly the same cases as before. No `NameError`, no stale-`estimates` leak across per-site iterations (when `estimate == -1` the block is skipped but `estimates` is never read).

**2. `plan_costs` `v = list(v)` copy — VERIFIED SAFE (no bug).**
`/workspace/pantheon-sitehealth-emails:865-867`. The original mutated the caller's `v` (`v[-1] = estimate`); the extraction copies first. I checked every use of `v` in `main()` (L3203 definition, L3204/3205 `len(v)`, L3220 argument) — `v` is never read after the `plan_costs` call, and it is rebuilt fresh each site iteration (L3203, not aliased). So the lost mutation is unobservable.

**3. `op_lookup` closure — VERIFIED IDENTICAL.** `op_lookup(month)` returns the same `db_session.get(PantheonOverageProtection, {"site_id": site["id"], "month": datetime.date.fromisoformat(month + "-01")})`. It is defined and invoked synchronously within the same per-site iteration, so the `site`/`db_session` closure captures the correct values (no late-binding issue).

**4. `op_remaining` retroactive-waiver / cost model — VERIFIED IDENTICAL.** The per-month loop, the `-01` reset to 4, the decrement, `cost_by_month`, `cost_for_plan_months`, the `&lt; 12` median padding, `cost_same`, `costs_median` (with `overage_blocks(...)` replacing the inline `round(...)` — algebraically identical), `costs_best = max(...)`, and `median_visitors = np.median(...)` all match the deleted code character-for-character in semantics.

**5. `overage_blocks` extraction + `n_blocks` rename — VERIFIED CLEAN.** `/workspace/pantheon-sitehealth-emails:3133-3136`. The former local `overage_blocks` variable is fully renamed to `n_blocks`; `grep` confirms every remaining `overage_blocks` reference (L776/844/878/3133) is the module-level function, and `overage_blocks_text` is an unrelated string. No shadowing of the module name survives.

<result>I have enough to report. I recomputed the pinned cost arithmetic and verified the model/parser facts; findings below.

## Adversarial review — new tests under `/workspace/tests/`

I recomputed the pinned cost-model arithmetic in `test_plan_costs.py` (overage_blocks banker's-rounding cases, the retroactive 4-month waiver → `100+80*8`, the short-history extrapolation → `100+480+480`, the estimate substitution → `round(10.5)=10` blocks → 400) and the `overage_blocks` literals in `test_plan_math.py`. All expected values are arithmetically correct — no wrong hand-computed constants. The `allow_abbrev=False` argparse contract and the DB `PrimaryKeyConstraint(site_id, traffic_date)` both check out, so those tests are sound. The per-test fresh-`SourceFileLoader` fixtures (aws/cloudflare/portal/sitelens) genuinely isolate module globals, so the suspected cross-test leakage does not occur.

Candidate findings (ranked):

1. **`tests/unit/test_plan_costs.py:139-147` — `test_median_visitors_uses_estimate` is vacuous.** It builds `v = [1000,1000,1000,1000,1000]` and passes `estimate=999999`, then asserts `median_visitors == 1000`. The code does `v[-1] = estimate` before `np.median(v)`, but the median of an odd-length list of five identical values is unchanged when one value is swapped for a larger one — the middle element stays 1000. So the assertion passes **whether or not** the `v[-1]=estimate` line runs; deleting that line (the exact behavior the test name claims to verify) would not fail it. The test's own comment admits "middle value unaffected." To actually prove the swap, it needs an even-length `v` or a value whose replacement moves the median. **Fails to catch:** removal/breakage of the estimate substitution into `median_visitors`.

2. **`tests/integration/test_mime_structure.py:29-33` — assertion doesn't match the name.** `test_has_nonempty_plaintext_and_html` only asserts `text_parts[0].get_content().strip() != ""`; the HTML part is checked for existence (`html_parts` truthy) but never for non-empty content. **Fails to catch:** a regression that emits an empty/whitespace `text/html` body — the very thing "and_html" implies is guarded.

3. **`tests/integration/test_check_sitelens.py:50-77` — averaging is never exercised.** The two seeded score rows are identical (`_score(0.90,0.70,0.40,1.00,1)` and `...,2)`), so the comment "Averages -&gt; accessibility 90..." is not tested: any bug that stopped averaging across scans and instead used only the first/last row would produce the same 90/70/40/100 and still pass. It would catch a sum-not-divided bug but not a wrong-aggregation-across-rows bug. Use differing per-row scores whose mean differs from any single row.

4. **`tests/e2e/test_recommendation_e2e.py:46-62` — "exercises plan_costs" but never checks its output.** Despite the docstring ("actually exercises the extracted plan_costs cost model end to end"), the test only asserts `returncode == 0`, absence of "Traceback"/"months more data", and the literal template strings "Recommended Plan"/"Current Plan". It never asserts which plan is recommended or any cost. **Fails to catch:** a plan_costs bug that yields a wrong-but-well-formed recommendation table.

5. **`tests/unit/test_plan_costs.py:76,89` (and `test_property_plan.py:75`) — `costs_best` checks are internal-consistency only.** `costs_best` is asserted to equal `max(cost_same[p], costs_median[p])` recomputed from the same call's other two return values. Since the implementation literally defines `costs_best` as that same max, the assertion can only catch a broken max op, not an incorrect `costs_best`; in `test_no_overage_costs_are_base` all three are trivially the base cost, making it doubly vacuous.

6. **`tests/unit/test_argparse_contract.py:28` — `smtp_username` default is a mirror tautology.** The parser default is `os.environ.get("USER", "")` (line 149-ff of the script) and the test asserts `ns.smtp_username == os.environ.get("USER", "")` — expected value derived from the identical source the code reads. A semantic change (e.g. to `getpass.getuser()`) would pass unnoticed in typical environments. Low severity, but it pins nothing beyond "the code reads USER."

Nothing was modified.</result>
<usage><subagent_tokens>82103</subagent_tokens><tool_uses>23</tool_uses><duration_ms>273445</duration_ms></usage>
</task-notification>

  "old_string": "def _resolve_config_arg(args, cwd):\n    \"\"\"Return the realpath of the effective --config/-c value, or None if not supplied.\"\"\"\n    value = None\n    i = 0\n    while i < len(args):\n        arg = args[i]\n        if arg in (\"--config\", \"-c\"):\n            value = args[i + 1] if i + 1 < len(args) else None\n            i += 2\n            continue\n        if arg.startswith(\"--config=\"):\n            value = arg.split(\"=\", 1)[1]\n        elif arg.startswith(\"-c=\"):\n            value = arg.split(\"=\", 1)[1]\n        i += 1\n    if value is None:\n        return None",
  "new_string": "def _resolve_config_arg(args, cwd):\n    \"\"\"Return the realpath of the effective --config/-c value, or None if not supplied.\n\n    Must mirror argparse's option parsing exactly, including stopping at ``--`` (everything\n    after it is positional): otherwise the guard could validate a config the program ignores\n    and fall open (a post-``--`` --config satisfying the allowlist while argparse uses the\n    default production config).\"\"\"\n    value = None\n    i = 0\n    while i < len(args):\n        arg = args[i]\n        if arg == \"--\":\n            break  # everything after \"--\" is positional, not an option — argparse ignores it\n        if arg in (\"--config\", \"-c\"):\n            value = args[i + 1] if i + 1 < len(args) else None\n            i += 2\n            continue\n        if arg.startswith(\"--config=\"):\n            value = arg.split(\"=\", 1)[1]\n        elif arg.startswith(\"-c=\"):\n            value = arg.split(\"=\", 1)[1]\n        elif arg.startswith(\"-c\") and len(arg) > 2:\n            value = arg[2:]  # glued short form: -cFOO  (argparse accepts this)\n        i += 1\n    if value is None:\n        return None"
}

## Assistant

The glued `-c<path>` test failed — but for an instructive reason: the path `/workspace/...minimal.toml` contains the letter **'a'** (in "workspace"), so the existing C1 forbidden-flag guard's `-a`-bundle heuristic (`"a" in token[1:]`) rejects it. So the glued form is already fail-closed via C1 and isn't a real use case. Finder-2's #4 (glued form) was explicitly "fail-closed, benign" — I over-fixed it. Let me revert the glued addition and drop that test, keeping the real `--` fix.

### ⚙ Tool call: `Edit`

```json
{
  "replace_all": false,
  "file_path": "/workspace/tests/conftest.py",
  "old_string": "        if arg.startswith(\"--config=\"):\n            value = arg.split(\"=\", 1)[1]\n        elif arg.startswith(\"-c=\"):\n            value = arg.split(\"=\", 1)[1]\n        elif arg.startswith(\"-c\") and len(arg) > 2:\n            value = arg[2:]  # glued short form: -cFOO  (argparse accepts this)\n        i += 1",
  "new_string": "        if arg.startswith(\"--config=\"):\n            value = arg.split(\"=\", 1)[1]\n        elif arg.startswith(\"-c=\"):\n            value = arg.split(\"=\", 1)[1]\n        i += 1"
}
```
